- `WIN` means the whole game is solved. Mid-run level completion is more likely to appear as a score increase while play continues.
- Strategies may transfer loosely across levels, but layouts and mechanics can change. Re-check the new board before repeating a plan.
- For `MOUSE`, pass `row` and `col` integer arguments. `row` is vertical position, `col` is horizontal position.


Python tool guidance:
- Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes.
- Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region of the board when `segmentation` is not enough; never use it to scan or summarize the whole board.
- Every `python` tool call starts fresh. Re-import modules or re-define any custom utility logic you need.
- The only importable standard-library modules are: bisect, collections, copy, fractions, functools, heapq, itertools, json, math, operator, random, re, statistics, string.
- The only tool is `python`; call it with one ephemeral `code` string.
- Always inspect `current_frame`, `history`, and `valid_actions` from Python instead of reasoning from the raw board by eye.
- For the most recent change, compare `previous_frame` to `current_frame`, or `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`. `history[-1].frame` is the current frame, so comparing it to `current_frame` only compares the board to itself.
- Maintain a compact working world model: what entities or regions exist, what actions seem to do, what the goal likely is, what remains uncertain, and what plan best fits the evidence so far.
- IMPORTANT: Especially when the game is about making an agent navigate to a target, it is usually safer to write an explicit search algorithm such as BFS. More generally, when the objective is understood but the best action order is unclear, pathfinding, flood fill, BFS, DFS, beam search, shortest-path search, limited action-sequence search, or custom heuristics are all valid.
- Optimize for the shortest reliable sequence that advances the current goal as described by your world model. If confidence is low, program a discriminating probe and revise the world model from the result.
- Once the important state variables and action effects are sufficiently understood, stop probing and search in the inferred state space.
- Inspect current and history frames from Python instead of describing frames freehand.
- Never print or echo full board frames. Return only compact derived summaries such as object lists, diffs, coordinates, counts, or tiny local crops.
- Keep tool-output context size minimal and decision-oriented so you can quickly compare before/after state. It's fine to write a lot of python code, just make the output short and interpretable
- A strong default loop is: summarize the board, infer the desired environment change, write a small scorer or search over candidate sequences, execute the best probe or plan with `action(...)`, then inspect again until you understand exactly what changed.
- For object tracking, match objects by color, overlap, bounding box proximity, area change, and edge contact rather than by exact coordinates alone.
- For frame diffs, summarize changed cells, color transitions, appearing/disappearing components, movement candidates, and small local row slices around the changed region.
- After every action, verify whether gameplay objects changed or whether only a timer, progress bar, or remaining-step bar moved. Do not treat HUD-only changes as evidence that the move worked.
- Use `print(...)` for compact summaries, or assign a final compact object to `result`.
- Call `action(...)` inside Python rather than returning action text in the chat.

# Extract symbol patterns from ASCII to compare visually
ascii_lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')

# Sky blue bar symbols (rows 41-45)
# Each symbol is 5x5, with spacing
# Let me extract each symbol's pattern

def extract_symbol(grid_lines, row_start, col_start, size=5):
    """Extract a size x size symbol pattern, replacing background with '.'"""
    pattern = []
    for r in range(row_start, row_start + size):
        row = grid_lines[r]
        pattern.append(row[col_start:col_start+size])
    return pattern

# Sky blue bar: rows 41-45
# From the ASCII, the sky blue bar starts at col 16 (after 16 G's)
# Each symbol is roughly 7 columns wide (5 for symbol + 2 for border)
# Let me find the exact positions from segmentation

seg = current_frame.segmentation
sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                    key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])

print("Sky blue bar symbols:")
for i, n in enumerate(sky_nodes):
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: rows {min_r}-{max_r}, cols {min_c}-{max_c}")
    # Extract pattern
    pattern = []
    for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
        row = ascii_lines[r]
        pattern.append(row[min_c:max_c+1])
    print(f"    {''.join(pattern)}")

print("\nPink bar symbols:")
for i, n in enumerate(pink_nodes):
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: rows {min_r}-{max_r}, cols {min_c}-{max_c}")
    pattern = []
    for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
        row = ascii_lines[r]
        pattern.append(row[min_c:max_c+1])
    print(f"    {''.join(pattern)}")

# Now let me compare shapes by normalizing the patterns
def shape_key(pattern):
    """Create a shape key by replacing background with '.' and foreground with '#'"""
    key = []
    for row in pattern:
        key_row = ''
        for ch in row:
            if ch == 'B':
                key_row += '#'
            else:
                key_row += '.'
        key.append(key_row)
    return '\n'.join(key)

print("\n\nShape comparison:")
sky_shapes = []
for n in sky_nodes:
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
    pattern = [ascii_lines[r][min_c:max_c+1] for r in range(min_r, max_r+1)]
    sky_shapes.append(shape_key(pattern))

pink_shapes = []
for n in pink_nodes:
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
    pattern = [ascii_lines[r][min_c:max_c+1] for r in range(min_r, max_r+1)]
    pink_shapes.append(shape_key(pattern))

for i in range(5):
    match = "MATCH" if sky_shapes[i] == pink_shapes[i] else "DIFFER"
    print(f"Pos {i+1}: {match}")
    if sky_shapes[i] != pink_shapes[i]:
        print(f"  Sky: {sky_shapes[i]}")
        print(f"  Pink: {pink_shapes[i]}")

Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- Important history semantics: when `history` is non-empty, `history[-1].frame` is the same latest/post-action board as `current_frame`. It is not the previous board. To inspect the state before the latest action, use `previous_frame` or `history[-2].frame` when available.
- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.
- `transitions` is a chronological list of actual action transitions, excluding the initial seeded frame. Each transition exposes `.action`, `.before_frame`, `.after_frame`, `.frame` (alias of `.after_frame`), and `.result`.
- `last_transition` is `transitions[-1]` or `None`. Its `.result` mirrors `last_action_result`; older transitions may have an empty `.result`. For before/after diffs, compare `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`; do not compare `current_frame` to `history[-1].frame`.
- `last_action_result` is the persisted result dict from the most recent `action(...)` call. It remains available across later Python inspection calls that do not call `action(...)`, and is `{}` before any action result exists. Read transition metadata from fields/keys such as `last_action_result['board_changed']`, `last_action_result['done']`, `last_action_result['level_completed']`, `last_action_result['game_over']`, `last_action_result['run_complete']`, `last_action_result['reward']`, and `last_action_result['valid_actions']`.

Visual-game guidance:
- Treat each board as a scene with objects, blockers, targets, adjacency, containment, motion, and symmetry.
- Game entities are usually be rendered as connected multi-tile shapes such as 2×2, 2×3, 3×3, or longer patterned structures. Sometime they might also be 1x1 tokens.- Some games are logic or layout puzzles with no explicit player avatar or controllable sprite on the board. Do not assume a player exists; the relevant state may be an object, region, cursor, selector, or whole-board configuration.
- Background colors are often white or gray/black-ish large regions, but not always. Verify background hypotheses by area, stability, and object boundaries rather than assuming them.
- In many games, a long horizontal or vertical line near an edge is a timer or remaining-steps bar. It often shrinks or changes each step. If you identify such a bar, do not get distracted by it or treat it as core gameplay state unless there is concrete evidence that it interacts with the puzzle mechanics.
A common failure mode is to mistake a segmented edge bar for clickable puzzle pieces. If a repeated strip of small blocks sits flush against the top, bottom, left, or right border and actions only change that strip while the interior board stays the same, classify it as HUD/timer state, not as an object to click through segment by segment. DON'T DO THIS!
- Use coordinates only to target actions or describe local evidence. Do not frame the objective as reaching a specific absolute row or column.
- Re-ground on the newest frame after any score increase or abrupt scene change; the returned board may already be the next level.
- `WIN` means the whole game is solved. Mid-run level completion is more likely to appear as a score increase while play continues.
- Strategies may transfer loosely across levels, but layouts and mechanics can change. Re-check the new board before repeating a plan.
- For `MOUSE`, pass `row` and `col` integer arguments. `row` is vertical position, `col` is horizontal position.


Python tool guidance:
- Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes.
- Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region of the board when `segmentation` is not enough; never use it to scan or summarize the whole board.
- Every `python` tool call starts fresh. Re-import modules or re-define any custom utility logic you need.
- The only importable standard-library modules are: bisect, collections, copy, fractions, functools, heapq, itertools, json, math, operator, random, re, statistics, string.
- The only tool is `python`; call it with one ephemeral `code` string.
- Always inspect `current_frame`, `history`, and `valid_actions` from Python instead of reasoning from the raw board by eye.
- For the most recent change, compare `previous_frame` to `current_frame`, or `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`. `history[-1].frame` is the current frame, so comparing it to `current_frame` only compares the board to itself.
- Maintain a compact working world model: what entities or regions exist, what actions seem to do, what the goal likely is, what remains uncertain, and what plan best fits the evidence so far.
- IMPORTANT: Especially when the game is about making an agent navigate to a target, it is usually safer to write an explicit search algorithm such as BFS. More generally, when the objective is understood but the best action order is unclear, pathfinding, flood fill, BFS, DFS, beam search, shortest-path search, limited action-sequence search, or custom heuristics are all valid.
- Optimize for the shortest reliable sequence that advances the current goal as described by your world model. If confidence is low, program a discriminating probe and revise the world model from the result.
- Once the important state variables and action effects are sufficiently understood, stop probing and search in the inferred state space.
- Inspect current and history frames from Python instead of describing frames freehand.
- Never print or echo full board frames. Return only compact derived summaries such as object lists, diffs, coordinates, counts, or tiny local crops.
- Keep tool-output context size minimal and decision-oriented so you can quickly compare before/after state. It's fine to write a lot of python code, just make the output short and interpretable
- A strong default loop is: summarize the board, infer the desired environment change, write a small scorer or search over candidate sequences, execute the best probe or plan with `action(...)`, then inspect again until you understand exactly what changed.
- For object tracking, match objects by color, overlap, bounding box proximity, area change, and edge contact rather than by exact coordinates alone.
- For frame diffs, summarize changed cells, color transitions, appearing/disappearing components, movement candidates, and small local row slices around the changed region.
- After every action, verify whether gameplay objects changed or whether only a timer, progress bar, or remaining-step bar moved. Do not treat HUD-only changes as evidence that the move worked.
- Use `print(...)` for compact summaries, or assign a final compact object to `result`.
- Call `action(...)` inside Python rather than returning action text in the chat.
- `action(...)` accepts an ordered list of one or more actions. Once your code has selected a reliable sequence, it is often useful to batch it.
- You can also call `action(...)` multiple times in one Python snippet, including inside loops. Each call updates the preloaded variables before execution continues.
- If an action result reports `game_over`, `run_complete`, `level_completed`, or `done`, stop acting immediately and re-ground on the next turn.

# Extract shape patterns from all transitions to build a hash-to-shape mapping
ascii_lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')

def get_symbol_shapes(frame):
    """Get shape patterns for pink bar symbols"""
    seg = frame.segmentation
    pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                        key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    shapes = []
    lines = frame.ascii.split('\n')
    for n in pink_nodes:
        cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
        rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
        min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
        min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
        pattern = []
        for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
            row = lines[r]
            pattern.append(row[min_c:max_c+1])
        # Normalize to shape key
        key = []
        for row in pattern:
            key_row = ''
            for ch in row:
                key_row += '#' if ch == 'B' else '.'
            key.append(key_row)
        shapes.append('\n'.join(key))
    return shapes

def get_arrow_pos(frame):
    """Get current arrow position (1-5)"""
    seg = frame.segmentation
    white_nodes = [n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'W' and n['boundary'][0][0] > 40]
    if not white_nodes:
        return None
    avg_col = sum(min(p[1] for p in n['boundary']) for n in white_nodes) / len(white_nodes)
    if avg_col < 20: return 1
    elif avg_col < 27: return 2
    elif avg_col < 34: return 3
    elif avg_col < 41: return 4
    else: return 5

# Build hash-to-shape mapping from transitions
hash_to_shape = {}
for t in transitions:
    pos = get_arrow_pos(t.after_frame)
    if pos is None:
        continue
    shapes = get_symbol_shapes(t.after_frame)
    h = t.after_frame.segmentation['nodes'][0]['hash']  # dummy
    # Get the hash for the symbol at this position
    seg = t.after_frame.segmentation
    pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                        key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    if pos-1 < len(pink_nodes):
        h = pink_nodes[pos-1]['hash']
        hash_to_shape[h[:8]] = shapes[pos-1]

print(f"Observed {len(hash_to_shape)} unique hash-to-shape mappings")
for h, s in sorted(hash_to_shape.items()):
    print(f"  {h}: {s}")

# Get current sky blue target shapes
seg = current_frame.segmentation
sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
sky_shapes = []
for n in sky_nodes:
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
    pattern = []
    for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
        row = ascii_lines[r]
        pattern.append(row[min_c:max_c+1])
    key = []
    for row in pattern:
        key_row = ''
        for ch in row:
            key_row += '#' if ch == 'B' else '.'
        key.append(key_row)
    sky_shapes.append('\n'.join(key))

print(f"\nSky blue target shapes:")
for i, s in enumerate(sky_shapes):
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: {s}")

# Now check which position cycles contain matching shapes
# From earlier: pos cycles
pos1_hashes = {'04a8e75f', '6610c6e3', '8b720570', 'a2774f59', 'b4edb3fa', 'cddd7d2c', 'f4469c24'}
pos2_hashes = {'3ad80649', '4d73d897', '886b69c2', '9f50b466', 'c66a83c4', 'f374da18', 'fb80c9b2'}
pos3_hashes = {'2c0adb75', '2c1efde5', '5fcaa599', '6f89cc49', 'b4edb3fa', 'cddd7d2c', 'f4469c24'}

    pos_hashes = all_pos_hashes[pos_idx]
    for h in pos_hashes:

# Let me extract top grid symbol shapes and compare to sky blue targets
ascii_lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')

# Top grid: rows 4-9, 13-18, 22-27 (3 rows of 4 symbols each)
# Each symbol is in a 7x7 box (including border)
# Sky blue boxes: cols 13-19, 33-39
# Pink boxes: cols 21-27, 43-49

seg = current_frame.segmentation

# Find all top grid symbol nodes (black nodes in top area)
top_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and n['boundary'][0][0] < 33], 
                   key=lambda n: (n['boundary'][0][0] // 8 * 8, n['boundary'][0][1]))

# Actually, let me find the box backgrounds first
top_boxes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] in ('S', 'P') and n['boundary'][0][0] < 33],
                   key=lambda n: (n['boundary'][0][0], n['boundary'][0][1]))

print(f"Top grid boxes: {len(top_boxes)}")
for i, box in enumerate(top_boxes):
    rows = [p[0] for p in box['boundary']]
    cols = [p[1] for p in box['boundary']]
    min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    # Extract the symbol inside (excluding border)
    pattern = []
    for r in range(min_r+1, max_r):
        row = ascii_lines[r]
        pattern.append(row[min_c+1:max_c])
    # Normalize
    key = []
    for row in pattern:
        key_row = ''
        for ch in row:
            key_row += '#' if ch == 'B' else '.'
        key.append(key_row)
    shape = '\n'.join(key)
    print(f"  Box {i+1} ({box['color']}): rows {min_r}-{max_r}, cols {min_c}-{max_c}")
    print(f"    {shape}")

# Now get sky blue target shapes again
sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
print(f"\nSky blue targets:")
for i, n in enumerate(sky_nodes):
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
    pattern = [ascii_lines[r][min_c:max_c+1] for r in range(min_r, max_r+1)]
    key = []
    for row in pattern:
        key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row)
        key.append(key_row)
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: {'\n'.join(key)}")

    cols = [p[1] for p in box['boundary']]

Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- Important history semantics: when `history` is non-empty, `history[-1].frame` is the same latest/post-action board as `current_frame`. It is not the previous board. To inspect the state before the latest action, use `previous_frame` or `history[-2].frame` when available.
- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.
- `transitions` is a chronological list of actual action transitions, excluding the initial seeded frame. Each transition exposes `.action`, `.before_frame`, `.after_frame`, `.frame` (alias of `.after_frame`), and `.result`.
- `last_transition` is `transitions[-1]` or `None`. Its `.result` mirrors `last_action_result`; older transitions may have an empty `.result`. For before/after diffs, compare `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`; do not compare `current_frame` to `history[-1].frame`.

If you identify such a bar, do not get distracted by it or treat it as core gameplay state unless there is concrete evidence that it interacts with the puzzle mechanics.

If a repeated strip of small blocks sits flush against the top, bottom, left, or right border and actions only change that strip while the interior board stays the same, classify it as HUD/timer state, not as an object to click through segment by segment. Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- Important history semantics: when `history` is non-empty, `history[-1].frame` is the same latest/post-action board as `current_frame`. It is not the previous board. To inspect the state before the latest action, use `previous_frame` or `history[-2].frame` when available.
- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.
- `transitions` is a chronological list of actual action transitions, excluding the initial seeded frame. Each transition exposes `.action`, `.before_frame`, `.after_frame`, `.frame` (alias of `.after_frame`), and `.result`.
- `last_transition` is `transitions[-1]` or `None`. Its `.result` mirrors `last_action_result`; older transitions may have an empty `.result`. For before/after diffs, compare `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`; do not compare `current_frame` to `history[-1].frame`.
- `last_action_result` is the persisted result dict from the most recent `action(...)` call. It remains available across later Python inspection calls that do not call `action(...)`, and is `{}` before any action result exists. Read transition metadata from fields/keys such as `last_action_result['board_changed']`, `last_action_result['done']`, `last_action_result['level_completed']`, `last_action_result['game_over']`, `last_action_result['run_complete']`, `last_action_result['reward']`, and `last_action_result['valid_actions']`.

- Call `action(actions)` to execute one or more real environment actions from Python.
- Pass `action(actions)` a list like `['LEFT']` or `[{'action': 'MOUSE', 'row': 4, 'col': 7}]`.

Visual-game guidance:
- Treat each board as a scene with objects, blockers, targets, adjacency, containment, motion, and symmetry.
- Game entities are usually be rendered as connected multi-tile shapes such as 2×2, 2×3, 3×3, or longer patterned structures. Sometime they might also be 1x1 tokens.- Some games are logic or layout puzzles with no explicit player avatar or controllable sprite on the board. Do not assume a player exists; the relevant state may be an object, region, cursor, selector, or whole-board configuration.
- Background colors are often white or gray/black-ish large regions, but not always. Verify background hypotheses by area, stability, and object boundaries rather than assuming them.
- In many games, a long horizontal or vertical line near an edge is a timer or remaining-steps bar. It often shrinks or changes each step. If you identify such a bar, do not get distracted by it or treat it as core gameplay state unless there is concrete evidence that it interacts with the puzzle mechanics.
A common failure mode is to mistake a segmented edge bar for clickable puzzle pieces. If a repeated strip of small blocks sits flush against the top, bottom, left, or right border and actions only change that strip while the interior board stays the same, classify it as HUD/timer state, not as an object to click through segment by segment. DON'T DO THIS!
- Use coordinates only to target actions or describe local evidence. Do not frame the objective as reaching a specific absolute row or column.
- Re-ground on the newest frame after any score increase or abrupt scene change; the returned board may already be the next level.
- `WIN` means the whole game is solved. Mid-run level completion is more likely to appear as a score increase while play continues.
- Strategies may transfer loosely across levels, but layouts and mechanics can change. Re-check the new board before repeating a plan.
- For `MOUSE`, pass `row` and `col` integer arguments. `row` is vertical position, `col` is horizontal position.


Python tool guidance:
- Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes.
- Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region of the board when `segmentation` is not enough; never use it to scan or summarize the whole board.
- Every `python` tool call starts fresh. Re-import modules or re-define any custom utility logic you need.
- The only importable standard-library modules are: bisect, collections, copy, fractions, functools, heapq, itertools, json, math, operator, random, re, statistics, string.
- The only tool is `python`; call it with one ephemeral `code` string.
- Always inspect `current_frame`, `history`, and `valid_actions` from Python instead of reasoning from the raw board by eye.
- For the most recent change, compare `previous_frame` to `current_frame`, or `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`. `history[-1].frame` is the current frame, so comparing it to `current_frame` only compares the board to itself.
- Maintain a compact working world model: what entities or regions exist, what actions seem to do, what the goal likely is, what remains uncertain, and what plan best fits the evidence so far.
- IMPORTANT: Especially when the game is about making an agent navigate to a target, it is usually safer to write an explicit search algorithm such as BFS. More generally, when the objective is understood but the best action order is unclear, pathfinding, flood fill, BFS, DFS, beam search, shortest-path search, limited action-sequence search, or custom heuristics are all valid.
- Optimize for the shortest reliable sequence that advances the current goal as described by your world model. If confidence is low, program a discriminating probe and revise the world model from the result.
- Once the important state variables and action effects are sufficiently understood, stop probing and search in the inferred state space.

Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- Important history semantics: when `history` is non-empty, `history[-1].frame` is the same latest/post-action board as `current_frame`. It is not the previous board. To inspect the state before the latest action, use `previous_frame` or `history[-2].frame` when available.
- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.
- `transitions` is a chronological list of actual action transitions, excluding the initial seeded frame. Each transition exposes `.action`, `.before_frame`, `.after_frame`, `.frame` (alias of `.after_frame`), and `.result`.
- `last_transition` is `transitions[-1]` or `None`. Its `.result` mirrors `last_action_result`; older transitions may have an empty `.result`. For before/after diffs, compare `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`; do not compare `current_frame` to `history[-1].frame`.
- `last_action_result` is the persisted result dict from the most recent `action(...)` call. # Extract shapes for both bars and compare
ascii_lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')
seg = current_frame.segmentation

def get_bar_shapes(bar_nodes, lines):
    shapes = []
    for n in bar_nodes:
        cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
        rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
        min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
        min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
        pattern = []
        for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
            row = lines[r]
            pattern.append(row[min_c:max_c+1])
        key = []
        for row in pattern:
            key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row)
            key.append(key_row)
        shapes.append('\n'.join(key))
    return shapes

sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                    key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])

sky_shapes = get_bar_shapes(sky_nodes, ascii_lines)
pink_shapes = get_bar_shapes(pink_nodes, ascii_lines)

print("Sky bar shapes:")
for i, s in enumerate(sky_shapes):
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: {s}")

print("\nPink bar shapes:")
for i, s in enumerate(pink_shapes):
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: {s}")

print("\nComparison:")

    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: {match}")

Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- Important history semantics: when `history` is non-empty, `history[-1].frame` is the same latest/post-action board as `current_frame`. It is not the previous board. To inspect the state before the latest action, use `previous_frame` or `history[-2].frame` when available.
- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.
- `transitions` is a chronological list of actual action transitions, excluding the initial seeded frame. Each transition exposes `.action`, `.before_frame`, `.after_frame`, `.frame` (alias of `.after_frame`), and `.result`.
- `last_transition` is `transitions[-1]` or `None`. Its `.result` mirrors `last_action_result`; older transitions may have an empty `.result`. For before/after diffs, compare `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`; do not compare `current_frame` to `history[-1].frame`.
- `last_action_result` is the persisted result dict from the most recent `action(...)` call. It remains available across later Python inspection calls that do not call `action(...)`, and is `{}` before any action result exists. Read transition metadata from fields/keys such as `last_action_result['board_changed']`, `last_action_result['done']`, `last_action_result['level_completed']`, `last_action_result['game_over']`, `last_action_result['run_complete']`, `last_action_result['reward']`, and `last_action_result['valid_actions']`.

Visual-game guidance:
- Treat each board as a scene with objects, blockers, targets, adjacency, containment, motion, and symmetry.
- Game entities are usually be rendered as connected multi-tile shapes such as 2×2, 2×3, 3×3, or longer patterned structures. Sometime they might also be 1x1 tokens.- Some games are logic or layout puzzles with no explicit player avatar or controllable sprite on the board. Do not assume a player exists; the relevant state may be an object, region, cursor, selector, or whole-board configuration.
- Background colors are often white or gray/black-ish large regions, but not always. Verify background hypotheses by area, stability, and object boundaries rather than assuming them.
- In many games, a long horizontal or vertical line near an edge is a timer or remaining-steps bar. It often shrinks or changes each step. If you identify such a bar, do not get distracted by it or treat it as core gameplay state unless there is concrete evidence that it interacts with the puzzle mechanics.
A common failure mode is to mistake a segmented edge bar for clickable puzzle pieces. If a repeated strip of small blocks sits flush against the top, bottom, left, or right border and actions only change that strip while the interior board stays the same, classify it as HUD/timer state, not as an object to click through segment by segment. - `WIN` means the whole game is solved. Mid-run level completion is more likely to appear as a score increase while play continues.
- Strategies may transfer loosely across levels, but layouts and mechanics can change. Re-check the new board before repeating a plan.
- For `MOUSE`, pass `row` and `col` integer arguments. `row` is vertical position, `col` is horizontal position.


Python tool guidance:
- Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes.
- Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region of the board when `segmentation` is not enough; never use it to scan or summarize the whole board.
- Every `python` tool call starts fresh. Re-import modules or re-define any custom utility logic you need.
- The only importable standard-library modules are: bisect, collections, copy, fractions, functools, heapq, itertools, json, math, operator, random, re, statistics, string.
- The only tool is `python`; call it with one ephemeral `code` string.
- Always inspect `current_frame`, `history`, and `valid_actions` from Python instead of reasoning from the raw board by eye.
- For the most recent change, compare `previous_frame` to `current_frame`, or `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`. `history[-1].frame` is the current frame, so comparing it to `current_frame` only compares the board to itself.
- Maintain a compact working world model: what entities or regions exist, what actions seem to do, what the goal likely is, what remains uncertain, and what plan best fits the evidence so far.
- IMPORTANT: Especially when the game is about making an agent navigate to a target, it is usually safer to write an explicit search algorithm such as BFS. More generally, when the objective is understood but the best action order is unclear, pathfinding, flood fill, BFS, DFS, beam search, shortest-path search, limited action-sequence search, or custom heuristics are all valid.
- Optimize for the shortest reliable sequence that advances the current goal as described by your world model. If confidence is low, program a discriminating probe and revise the world model from the result.
- Once the important state variables and action effects are sufficiently understood, stop probing and search in the inferred state space.
- Inspect current and history frames from Python instead of describing frames freehand.
- Never print or echo full board frames. Return only compact derived summaries such as object lists, diffs, coordinates, counts, or tiny local crops.

# Build comprehensive hash-to-shape map from all transitions
# Then find which hash at each position matches the sky target

ascii_lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')

def extract_pink_shapes(frame):
    """Extract shapes for all 5 pink bar positions"""
    seg = frame.segmentation
    pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                        key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    lines = frame.ascii.split('\n')
    shapes = []
    for n in pink_nodes:
        cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
        rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
        min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
        min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
        pattern = []
        for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
            row = lines[r]
            pattern.append(row[min_c:max_c+1])
        key = []
        for row in pattern:
            key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row)
            key.append(key_row)
        shapes.append('\n'.join(key))
    return shapes

# Build hash-to-shape mapping from all transitions
hash_to_shape = {}
for t in transitions:
    seg = t.after_frame.segmentation
    pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                        key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    lines = t.after_frame.ascii.split('\n')
    for idx, n in enumerate(pink_nodes):
        h = n['hash']
        cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
        rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
        min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
        min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
        pattern = []
        for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
            row = lines[r]
            pattern.append(row[min_c:max_c+1])
        key = []
        for row in pattern:
            key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row)
            key.append(key_row)
        shape = '\n'.join(key)
        hash_to_shape[h] = shape

print(f"Total unique hashes observed: {len(hash_to_shape)}")

# Sky blue target shapes (from current frame)
seg = current_frame.segmentation
sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
sky_targets = []
for n in sky_nodes:
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
    pattern = []
    for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
        row = ascii_lines[r]
        pattern.append(row[min_c:max_c+1])
    key = []
    for row in pattern:
        key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row)
        key.append(key_row)
    sky_targets.append('\n'.join(key))

# For each position, find which hash produces the target shape
# First, build position-to-hashes mapping from transitions
pos_hashes = {1: set(), 2: set(), 3: set(), 4: set(), 5: set()}

for t in transitions:
    seg = t.after_frame.segmentation
    pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                        key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    for idx, n in enumerate(pink_nodes):
        pos_hashes[idx+1].add(n['hash'])

print(f"\nHashes per position:")
for pos, hashes in pos_hashes.items():
    print(f"  Pos {pos}: {len(hashes)} hashes")

# Check which target shapes can be matched
print(f"\nTarget matching:")
for pos_idx, target in enumerate(sky_targets):
    pos = pos_idx + 1
    found = False
    for h in pos_hashes[pos]:
        if h in hash_to_shape and hash_to_shape[h] == target:
            print(f"  Pos {pos}: MATCH hash {h[:8]}")
            found = True
            break
    if not found:

Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- Important history semantics: when `history` is non-empty, `history[-1].frame` is the same latest/post-action board as `current_frame`. It is not the previous board. To inspect the state before the latest action, use `previous_frame` or `history[-2].frame` when available.
- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.
- `transitions` is a chronological list of actual action transitions, excluding the initial seeded frame. Each transition exposes `.action`, `.before_frame`, `.after_frame`, `.frame` (alias of `.after_frame`), and `.result`.
- `last_transition` is `transitions[-1]` or `None`. Its `.result` mirrors `last_action_result`; older transitions may have an empty `.result`. For before/after diffs, compare `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`; do not compare `current_frame` to `history[-1].frame`.

Visual-game guidance:

Do not assume a player exists; the relevant state may be an object, region, cursor, selector, or whole-board configuration.
- Background colors are often white or gray/black-ish large regions, but not always. Verify background hypotheses by area, stability, and object boundaries rather than assuming them.
- In many games, a long horizontal or vertical line near an edge is a timer or remaining-steps bar. It often shrinks or changes each step. If you identify such a bar, do not get distracted by it or treat it as core gameplay state unless there is concrete evidence that it interacts with the puzzle mechanics.
A common failure mode is to mistake a segmented edge bar for clickable puzzle pieces. If a repeated strip of small blocks sits flush against the top, bottom, left, or right border and actions only change that strip while the interior board stays the same, classify it as HUD/timer state, not as an object to click through segment by segment. # Correct extraction with proper row ranges
lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')

# Sky bar: rows 41-45
sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in current_frame.segmentation['nodes'] 
                    if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])

# Pink bar: rows 52-56  
pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in current_frame.segmentation['nodes'] 
                     if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                    key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])

def extract_shape(nodes, lines, row_range):
    shapes = []
    for n in nodes:
        cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
        min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
        key = []
        for r in row_range:
            row = lines[r]
            key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row[min_c:max_c+1])
            key.append(key_row)
        shapes.append('\n'.join(key))
    return shapes

sky_shapes = extract_shape(sky_nodes, lines, range(41, 46))
pink_shapes = extract_shape(pink_nodes, lines, range(52, 57))

print("Sky targets:")
for i, s in enumerate(sky_shapes):
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: {s}")

print("\nPink current:")
for i, s in enumerate(pink_shapes):
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: {s}")

print("\nComparison:")
for i in range(5):
    match = "MATCH" if sky_shapes[i] == pink_shapes[i] else "DIFFER"
    print(f"  Pos {i+1}: {match}")

hash_to_shape = {}
for t in transitions:
    seg = t.after_frame.segmentation
    pn = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    tl = t.after_frame.ascii.split('\n')
    for idx, n in enumerate(pn):

        key = []
        for r in range(52, 57):
            row = tl[r]
            key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row[min_c:max_c+1])
            key.append(key_row)
        hash_to_shape[n['hash']] = '\n'.join(key)

# Look for sky blue and pink boxes in the top area
top_boxes = [n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] in ('S', 'P') and n['boundary'][0][0] < 30]

for n in top_boxes:
    rows = [p[0] for p in n['boundary']]
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    print(f"  Color={n['color']}, rows {min(rows)}-{max(rows)}, cols {min(cols)}-{max(cols)}, hash={n['hash'][:8]}, children={n['children']}")

# Let me extract the symbol shapes from the children

symbol_shapes = {}
for n in top_boxes:
    for child_id in n['children']:
        child = seg['nodes'][child_id]
        if child['color'] == 'B':
            cols = [p[1] for p in child['boundary']]
            rows = [p[0] for p in child['boundary']]
            min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
            min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
            key = []
            for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
                row = lines[r]
                key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row[min_c:max_c+1])
                key.append(key_row)
            shape = '\n'.join(key)
            symbol_shapes[(n['color'], n['hash'][:8])] = shape
            print(f"  Box {n['color']} hash {n['hash'][:8]}: child hash {child['hash'][:8]}")
            print(f"    {shape}")

Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.

- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.

<parameter=code>
# Let me check the top grid sky blue symbols more carefully
# and see if sky targets match any of them (including pink symbols)

lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')
seg = current_frame.segmentation

# Sky targets (from bottom sky blue bar)
sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
sky_targets = []
for n in sky_nodes:
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    key = []
    for r in range(41, 46):
        row = lines[r]
        key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row[min_c:max_c+1])
        key.append(key_row)
    sky_targets.append('\n'.join(key))

# Top grid box children (both sky blue and pink boxes)
top_boxes = [n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] in ('S', 'P') and n['boundary'][0][0] < 30 and len(n['children']) > 0]
top_boxes = sorted(top_boxes, key=lambda n: (n['boundary'][0][0] // 8, n['boundary'][0][1]))

# Extract child shapes
all_top_symbols = []
for n in top_boxes:
    for child_id in n['children']:
        child = seg['nodes'][child_id]
        if child['color'] == 'B':
            cols = [p[1] for p in child['boundary']]
            rows = [p[0] for p in child['boundary']]
            min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
            min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
            key = []
            for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
                row = lines[r]
                key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row[min_c:max_c+1])
                key.append(key_row)
            shape = '\n'.join(key)
            all_top_symbols.append((n['color'], n['hash'][:8], child['hash'][:8], shape))

# Compare sky targets to ALL top symbols (both sky blue and pink)
print("Comparing sky targets to all top grid symbols:")
for pos_idx, target in enumerate(sky_targets):
    print(f"\nSky target pos {pos_idx+1}:")
    matched = False
    for color, box_hash, child_hash, shape in all_top_symbols:
        if shape == target:
            print(f"  MATCH: {color} box {box_hash}, child {child_hash}")
            matched = True
    if not matched:
        print(f"  NO MATCH")

# Also check: do the sky targets match the pink bar's available symbols?
# Build hash-to-shape from transitions
hash_to_shape = {}
for t in transitions:
    seg2 = t.after_frame.segmentation
    pn = sorted([n for n in seg2['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    tl = t.after_frame.ascii.split('\n')
    for idx, n in enumerate(pn):
        cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
        min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
        key = []
        for r in range(52, 57):
            row = tl[r]
            key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row[min_c:max_c+1])
            key.append(key_row)
        hash_to_shape[n['hash']] = '\n'.join(key)

print("\nComparing sky targets to available pink bar symbols:")
for pos_idx, target in enumerate(sky_targets):
    print(f"\nSky target pos {pos_idx+1}:")
    for h, shape in hash_to_shape.items():
        if shape == target:
            print(f"  MATCH: hash {h[:8]}")
            break
    else:
        print(f"  NO MATCH in {len(hash_to_shape)} observed hashes")

Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- Important history semantics: when `history` is non-empty, `history[-1].frame` is the same latest/post-action board as `current_frame`. It is not the previous board. To inspect the state before the latest action, use `previous_frame` or `history[-2].frame` when available.
- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.
- `transitions` is a chronological list of actual action transitions, excluding the initial seeded frame. Each transition exposes `.action`, `.before_frame`, `.after_frame`, `.frame` (alias of `.after_frame`), and `.result`.
- `last_transition` is `transitions[-1]` or `None`. Its `.result` mirrors `last_action_result`; older transitions may have an empty `.result`. For before/after diffs, compare `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`; do not compare `current_frame` to `history[-1].frame`.
- `last_action_result` is the persisted result dict from the most recent `action(...)` call. It remains available across later Python inspection calls that do not call `action(...)`, and is `{}` before any action result exists. Read transition metadata from fields/keys such as `last_action_result['board_changed']`, `last_action_result['done']`, `last_action_result['level_completed']`, `last_action_result['game_over']`, `last_action_result['run_complete']`, `last_action_result['reward']`, and `last_action_result['valid_actions']`.
- `valid_actions` is the current list of valid action names.
- Call `action(actions)` to execute one or more real environment actions from Python.
- Pass `action(actions)` a list like `['LEFT']` or `[{'action': 'MOUSE', 'row': 4, 'col': 7}]`.
- One action usually returns one frame, but a single action can result in a short multi-frame animation.
- After `action(actions)` returns, `current_frame`, `previous_frame`, `history`, `transitions`, `valid_actions`, and `last_action_result` are refreshed.

- In many games, a long horizontal or vertical line near an edge is a timer or remaining-steps bar. It often shrinks or changes each step. If you identify such a bar, do not get distracted by it or treat it as core gameplay state unless there is concrete evidence that it interacts with the puzzle mechanics.
A common failure mode is to mistake a segmented edge bar for clickable puzzle pieces. If a repeated strip of small blocks sits flush against the top, bottom, left, or right border and actions only change that strip while the interior board stays the same, classify it as HUD/timer state, not as an object to click through segment by segment. # Let me try a completely different approach
# Check if the sky bar symbols match the top grid PINK symbols (not sky blue)

lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')
seg = current_frame.segmentation

# Sky targets
sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
sky_targets = []
for n in sky_nodes:
    cols = [p[1] for p in n['boundary']]
    min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
    key = []
    for r in range(41, 46):
        row = lines[r]
        key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row[min_c:max_c+1])
        key.append(key_row)
    sky_targets.append('\n'.join(key))

# Top grid pink box children
pink_boxes = [n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'P' and n['boundary'][0][0] < 30 and len(n['children']) > 0]
pink_boxes = sorted(pink_boxes, key=lambda n: (n['boundary'][0][0] // 8, n['boundary'][0][1]))

pink_child_hashes = []
for n in pink_boxes:
    for child_id in n['children']:
        child = seg['nodes'][child_id]
        if child['color'] == 'B':
            cols = [p[1] for p in child['boundary']]
            rows = [p[0] for p in child['boundary']]
            min_c, max_c = min(cols), max(cols)
            min_r, max_r = min(rows), max(rows)
            key = []
            for r in range(min_r, max_r+1):
                row = lines[r]
                key_row = ''.join('#' if ch == 'B' else '.' for ch in row[min_c:max_c+1])
                key.append(key_row)
            shape = '\n'.join(key)
            pink_child_hashes.append((n['hash'][:8], child['hash'][:8], shape))

print("Top grid pink symbols:")
for box_h, child_h, shape in pink_child_hashes:
    print(f"  Box {box_h}, child {child_h}:")
    print(f"    {shape}")

# Compare sky targets to pink child hashes
print("\nComparing sky targets to pink child hashes:")
for pos_idx, target in enumerate(sky_targets):
    print(f"\nSky target pos {pos_idx+1}:")
    for box_h, child_h, shape in pink_child_hashes:
        if shape == target:
            print(f"  MATCH: child hash {child_h}")
    else:
        print(f"  NO MATCH")

# Now let's check: which pink child hashes are available at each position?
pos_hashes = {1: set(), 2: set(), 3: set(), 4: set(), 5: set()}
for t in transitions:
    seg2 = t.after_frame.segmentation
    pn = sorted([n for n in seg2['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    for idx, n in enumerate(pn):
        pos_hashes[idx+1].add(n['hash'])

print("\nPink child hashes available at each position:")
for box_h, child_h, shape in pink_child_hashes:
    available_at = [pos for pos, hashes in pos_hashes.items() if child_h in hashes]
    print(f"  Child {child_h}: available at positions {available_at}")

# Compare sky bar symbol HASHES to top grid symbol hashes
lines = current_frame.ascii.split('\n')
seg = current_frame.segmentation

# Sky bar symbol hashes
sky_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 40 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 47], 
                   key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
sky_hashes = [n['hash'] for n in sky_nodes]
print("Sky bar symbol hashes:", sky_hashes)

# Top grid sky blue box child hashes
sky_boxes = [n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'S' and n['boundary'][0][0] < 30 and len(n['children']) > 0]
sky_boxes = sorted(sky_boxes, key=lambda n: (n['boundary'][0][0] // 8, n['boundary'][0][1]))
sky_child_hashes = []
for n in sky_boxes:
    for child_id in n['children']:
        child = seg['nodes'][child_id]
        if child['color'] == 'B':
            sky_child_hashes.append(child['hash'])
print("Top grid sky blue child hashes:", sky_child_hashes)

# Top grid pink box child hashes
pink_boxes = [n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'P' and n['boundary'][0][0] < 30 and len(n['children']) > 0]
pink_boxes = sorted(pink_boxes, key=lambda n: (n['boundary'][0][0] // 8, n['boundary'][0][1]))
pink_child_hashes = []
for n in pink_boxes:
    for child_id in n['children']:
        child = seg['nodes'][child_id]
        if child['color'] == 'B':
            pink_child_hashes.append(child['hash'])
print("Top grid pink child hashes:", pink_child_hashes)

# Check hash overlaps
print("\nSky bar hashes matching top grid sky blue children:")
for sh in sky_hashes:
    if sh in sky_child_hashes:
        print(f"  MATCH: {sh}")
    else:
        print(f"  NO MATCH: {sh}")

print("\nSky bar hashes matching top grid pink children:")
for sh in sky_hashes:
    if sh in pink_child_hashes:
        print(f"  MATCH: {sh}")
    else:
        print(f"  NO MATCH: {sh}")

# Check: do the sky bar hashes match the pink bar available hashes?
all_available = set()
for t in transitions:
    seg2 = t.after_frame.segmentation
    pn = sorted([n for n in seg2['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    for n in pn:
        all_available.add(n['hash'])

print("\nSky bar hashes matching available pink bar hashes:")
for sh in sky_hashes:
    if sh in all_available:
        print(f"  MATCH: {sh}")
    else:
        print(f"  NO MATCH: {sh}")

Runtime variables inside every `python` tool call:
- `current_frame` is a lightweight frame view for the latest environment state.
- `current_frame` exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- `current_frame.ascii` is a single newline-delimited string containing the latest board rendered with the letter-coded ARC color symbols.
- `current_frame.segmentation` parses the board into objects. It returns `{'nodes': [...], 'adjacency_list': [...]}`.
- Each node in `segmentation['nodes']` is one 4-connected same-color object with: `id` (index, ordered top-most-left-most), `color` (ARC color character), `hash` (a signature of the object's color and shape that ignores its position -- equal hashes mean the same object regardless of where it is, so use it to track an object across frames or to spot multiple identical objects in one frame), `pixels` (cell count), `boundary` (clockwise outer-perimeter corner points as `[row, col]`), and `children` (ids of objects fully enclosed by this one).
- `segmentation['adjacency_list']` is a list of `[i, j]` node-id pairs whose objects share an edge.
- `current_frame.step` is the current environment step count.
- `current_frame.level` is the current level number.
- `current_frame.shape` is a `(rows, cols)` tuple.
- The raw numeric grid is intentionally not exposed. Use `current_frame.segmentation` as your primary view of the board -- objects, colors, shapes, containment, adjacency, and cross-frame object hashes. Use `current_frame.ascii` only to read a small, specific region; do not scan the whole board with it.
- `history` is a chronological list of action/frame snapshots.
- `history` is a Python list of objects, not a dict.
- Each history entry exposes only `.action` and `.frame`; entries are not subscriptable like `entry['action']`.
- Each `history[i].frame` is the frame after `history[i].action`; each frame exposes only `.ascii`, `.step`, `.level`, `.shape`, and `.segmentation`.
- Important history semantics: when `history` is non-empty, `history[-1].frame` is the same latest/post-action board as `current_frame`. It is not the previous board. To inspect the state before the latest action, use `previous_frame` or `history[-2].frame` when available.
- `previous_frame` is the frame before the most recent real environment action, or `None` if no previous frame is available.
- `last_action` is the most recent real environment action name/display, or `None` before any real action.
- `last_action_frame` is the post-action frame for `last_action`; it matches `current_frame` after a real action.
- `transitions` is a chronological list of actual action transitions, excluding the initial seeded frame. Each transition exposes `.action`, `.before_frame`, `.after_frame`, `.frame` (alias of `.after_frame`), and `.result`.
- `last_transition` is `transitions[-1]` or `None`. Its `.result` mirrors `last_action_result`; older transitions may have an empty `.result`. For before/after diffs, compare `last_transition.before_frame` to `last_transition.after_frame`; do not compare `current_frame` to `history[-1].frame`.

If you identify such a bar, do not get distracted by it or treat it as core gameplay state unless there is concrete evidence that it interacts with the puzzle mechanics.
A common failure mode is to mistake a segmented edge bar for clickable puzzle pieces. If a repeated strip of small blocks sits flush against the top, bottom, left, or right border and actions only change that strip while the interior board stays the same, classify it as HUD/timer state, not as an object to click through segment by segment. # Let me check the cursor position and build a complete map of position->value->UP/DOWN transitions
seg = current_frame.segmentation

# Find cursor (white arrow)
cursor_nodes = [n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'W']

for n in cursor_nodes:
    print(f"  Color: {n['color']}, pixels: {n['pixels']}, boundary: {n['boundary'][:3]}...")

# Current pink bar state
pink_nodes = sorted([n for n in seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                    key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
print(f"\nCurrent pink bar: {[n['hash'][:8] for n in pink_nodes]}")

# Build complete transition map for each position
# From transitions, record: (position, before_hash, action, after_hash)
pos_transitions = {1: {}, 2: {}, 3: {}, 4: {}, 5: {}}
for t in transitions:
    before_seg = t.before_frame.segmentation
    after_seg = t.after_frame.segmentation
    action_name = t.action
    
    before_pink = sorted([n for n in before_seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                         key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    after_pink = sorted([n for n in after_seg['nodes'] if n['color'] == 'B' and 50 <= n['boundary'][0][0] < 58], 
                        key=lambda n: n['boundary'][0][1])
    
    if len(before_pink) == 5 and len(after_pink) == 5:
        for i in range(5):
            if before_pink[i]['hash'] != after_pink[i]['hash']:
                pos = i + 1
                before_h = before_pink[i]['hash'][:8]
                after_h = after_pink[i]['hash'][:8]
                if before_h not in pos_transitions[pos]:
                    pos_transitions[pos][before_h] = []
                pos_transitions[pos][before_h].append((action_name, after_h))

print("\nPosition transition maps:")
for pos, trans in pos_transitions.items():
    print(f"\nPos {pos}:")
    for before_h, actions in sorted(trans.items()):
        print(f"  {before_h} -> {actions}")
